ACS Nano ACS Nano eScience">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, it remained an open question on how to stabilize the interphases with desired structures and components, and whether we could establish the solvation-interphase-performance relationship. We believe the current work here contributes to a molecular-level understanding of establishing the relationship and offers a new perspective on stabilizing SEI and CEI to promote cell performance under harsh conditions.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202403138-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In this work, the components and structures of CEI and SEI have been tailored through carboxylic ester- and SN-based electrolytes. The SEI on hard carbon anodes rich with NaF shows improved homogeneity and mechanical stability and meanwhile, the inhibited formation of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> restrains SEI growth. Furthermore, the F-/N-inorganics rich CEI derived from the SN and FEC decomposition synergistically leads to thin and robust CEI. Consequently, the NVOPF cell with the tailored CEI achieves 83.3% capacity retention over 3000 cycles measured at 1 C, and a prototype full cell of NVOPF||HC sustains over 500 cycles at a current density of 1 C. This work demonstrates a promising co-solvation strategy to stabilize cell interphases with desired thickness and components for the long operation of high-energy-density SIBs under harsh conditions. We expect that the molecular-selected strategy can be extended to other energy storage systems with similar chemical challenges at high voltage.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202403138-sec-0080-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0090">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0100">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403138-sec-0110-title"> Preparation of Electrolytes and Electrodes</h4>
                  
                  <p>The benchmark carbonate electrolyte consisting of 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> (Battery-grade, Guangdong Candle New Energy Technology) dissolved in EC (battery grade, TCI)/PC (battery grade, TCI) (1:1, in volume) was prepared in the Ar-filled glovebox, in which the level of O<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O was below 0.1&nbsp;ppm. The carboxylic ester-SN based electrolytes were prepared by mixing 1&nbsp;mol NaClO<sub>4</sub> in MA or EA (battery-grade, TCI)/SN (&gt;98%, Guangdong Candle New Energy Technology)/FEC (battery grade, TCI) with volume ratio of 47.5:47.5:5. Prior to the electrolyte preparation, NaClO<sub>4</sub> was dried at 120&nbsp;°C for 24&nbsp;h under vacuum condition, and all the solvents were dried using 4 A molecular sieves (Sigma–Aldrich) for 2 days in the Ar-filled glovebox. The commercial hard carbon (HC) (Kuraray Co) was used as received without any treatment. The electrodes of HC were prepared by first casting a slurry of active material/PVDF/Super-P (8/1/1, in weight) in NMP solvent on Al foil, and then vacuum-dried at 120&nbsp;°C overnight. The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F (NVOPF) cathode was synthesized as previously reported,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403138-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403138-bib-0030_R_d8242329e1674" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Energy Mater. Adv.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> in which a solution with NaH<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O, NaF and NH<sub>3</sub>·H<sub>2</sub>O (V:P:F = 1:3:1.7, in molar ratio) was mixed with solution VOSO<sub>4</sub>·<i>x</i>H<sub>2</sub>O, followed by calcinating at 450&nbsp;°C for 0.5&nbsp;h under Ar flow. The procedure for preparing NVOPF electrodes remained the same as that for HC electrodes except for the difference in the slurry formulation (i.e., NVOPF:Ketjen Black:PVDF = 7:2:1, in weight).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403138-sec-0120-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>2025-type coin cells were fabricated with sodium metal (99.8%, Sigma–Aldrich) or HC anodes, a separator (GF/D, Whatman), and ≈150&nbsp;µL electrolyte in each cell in an argon-filled glove box (O<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O &lt;1&nbsp;ppm). All electrochemical performance of cells was evaluated by a standard battery tester (Neware, CT4008). Both the electrodes of NVOPF and HC were punched into circular discs with a diameter of 10&nbsp;mm. The half cells with NVOPF and HC as working electrodes were cycled between 2 and 4.3&nbsp;V (1 C = 120&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and 0 and 2.5&nbsp;V (current density: 30 and 300&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>), respectively. Prior to assembling the full cells, three cycles were performed on both NVOPF and HC electrodes based on the half-cell configurations (i.e., NVOPF||Na and Na||HC) for activation. The N/P ratio for the NVOPF||HC full cells was set at ≈1.3, and they were operated between 1.2 and 4.1&nbsp;V with the C-rate based on the NVOPF mass (1 C = 120 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was conducted on an electrochemical workstation (Gamry, 5000 E) within a frequency of 100&nbsp;kHz–0.1&nbsp;Hz. Linear sweeping voltammetry (LSV) measurements were also carried out to assess the oxidation durability of the electrolytes (Gamry, 5000 E). With a scanning rate of 1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, the LSV measurement started at the open circuit voltage and ended at 5.5&nbsp;V, where the metallic Na and stainless steel were employed as reference/counter electrode and working electrode, respectively.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403138-sec-0130-title"> Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>Raman spectra (WiTech alpha 300R, 532&nbsp;nm laser light) were used to reveal the solvation structure of three electrolytes, including Na coordination with SN and the intermolecular interaction between SN and MA/EA solvent. Further, nuclear magnetic resonance (NMR, Bruker, 600&nbsp;MHz Ultrashield) was also conducted by coaxial NMR tube to examine the difference in the solvation environment of Na<sup>+</sup> in the electrolytes. 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaCl-D<sub>2</sub>O was used as an internal standard during NMR measurement. The viscosity of electrolytes was measured at room temperature, and the thermogravimetric (TG) analysis was conducted under N<sub>2</sub> by an instrument of SDT Q600 V20.9 Build 20. For the post-mortem interphase characterization, the NVOPF electrodes (after 300 cycles at 1 C) and the cycled HC electrodes (250 cycles at 150&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) were disassembled in a high-pure Ar-filled glove box. The residual electrolytes (salt and solvents) on the collected electrodes were rinsed off using the dimethyl carbonate (DMC) solvent, and the procedures followed the order of soaking in DMC for 1–2&nbsp;min, rinsing with DMC for 4 times, and naturally dried in the glove box. Afterwards, the electrodes were removed from the glove box for the post-mortem characterizations, wherein all electrodes were first placed into airtight containers that were well sealed to avoid exposure to air and/or any contaminants during transfer. The measurement of transmission electron microscopy (TEM, Thermo Fisher Talos F200s) was performed to examine the surface morphologies and interphase thickness. The surface components were determined by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, Thermo Fisher Nexs) spectra with Ar<sup>+</sup> clusters sputtered for depth analysis. For calibration, the C 1s peak of 284.8&nbsp;eV was used as the reference.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403138-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403138-sec-0140-title"> Computational Methods</h4>
                  
                  <p>Molecular dynamics (MD) simulations were carried out by using the Gromacs 2021 program.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403138-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403138-bib-0031_R_d8242329e1749" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - SoftwareX">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The initial electrolyte model was generated with a packmol package.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403138-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403138-bib-0032_R_d8242329e1754" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - J. Comput. Chem.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Three atomistic modeling systems were constructed as follows: 1) EC/PC electrolyte (50 NaClO<sub>4</sub>, 361 EC, 284&nbsp;PC); 2) EA-SN-FEC electrolyte (100 NaClO<sub>4</sub>, 462 EA, 559 SN, 66 FEC); 3) MA-SN-FEC electrolyte (100 NaClO<sub>4</sub>, 546 MA, 533 SN, 63 FEC). Periodic boundary conditions were used in all dimensions. An energy minimization was performed for the initial model by using the steepest descent method. Afterward, MD simulations were performed in the canonical ensemble (NVT) to generate velocities and structural parameters for the following equilibrium process in the isothermal-isobaric ensemble (NPT) using the Berendson barostat. After the initial model came to an equilibrium state, 100&nbsp;ns MD simulations in the NPT ensemble were performed using the Berendsen barostat and V-rescale thermostat. The large-scale MD simulations for the electrolyte model proceeded at 300&nbsp;K and 1&nbsp;bar with a timestep of 2&nbsp;fs.</p>
                  
                  <p>Representative solvation structures were extracted from extensive atomistic simulation trajectories and were used as starting configurations for subsequent quantum chemistry calculations. Quantum chemistry calculations were performed to optimize molecular geometries of solvent molecules using the Gaussian 16 package<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403138-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403138-bib-0033_R_d8242329e1769" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> at B3LYP/6-311+G(d) level of theory. Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof functional was used to specify the exchange-correlation treatments and Grimme's D3 dispersion correction was added in all calculations. Molecular forces were determined by the general Amber force field (GAFF).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403138-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403138-bib-0034_R_d8242329e1774" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - J. Comput. Chem.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Topology files and Lennard-Jones parameters of molecules and ions were produced by using the visual force field derivation toolkit (VFFDT) software.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403138-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403138-bib-0035_R_d8242329e1779" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Chem. Inf. Model.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Atomic partial charges were calculated by fitting the electrostatic potential. DFT-D3 calculations package were performed to optimize the molecular geometry of the obtained solvation structures and then to calculate the electrostatic potential (ESP), and relevant HOMO-LUMO energies. The atomic configurations were analyzed by using open visualization tool software (OVITO),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403138-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403138-bib-0036_R_d8242329e1785" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Modell. Simul. Mater. Sci. Eng.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> including the pair correlation function and Na<sup>+</sup> ion solvation structure analysis.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
